Local News

Zhabei Continues to Enjoy Peace

Japanese Troops Once Went to Move Relics

Rumors Caused Have Been Settled

Rumors have been circulating in the city for days that Japanese troops are again conducting demonstrations in the Zhabei area. Therefore, the National Salvation Federation has requested the municipal government to increase defense in Zhabei and other areas. At around 11:00 AM yesterday, there was a sudden rumor that a large number of Japanese troops were passing through Zhabei, and the situation suddenly became tense. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency made a special trip to the fifth district of Zhabei and the Zhabei area to thoroughly understand the facts. After detailed investigation, it was learned that the rumors were completely based on misunderstandings. The details obtained are recorded below:

Moving Relic Silk Nets Causes Many People to Misunderstand

The reporter conducted a detailed investigation yesterday in the area of Tiantong'an, Baoxing Road, and Qiujiang Road. It was learned that around the 25th, Japanese troops were collecting damaged silk nets and sandbags at the eastern end of the exit of Songhu Road and behind the Japanese Naval Landing Force Headquarters on Huanglu Road, and transporting them to the Pingliang Road yarn factory. As a result, nearby residents were unaware of the contents and became suspicious, saying that the Japanese Navy would take action in Zhabei. The rumors became more and more exaggerated, and it became truer and truer. Fortunately, the municipal public security bureau police officers at the scene immediately explained the situation to the residents, preventing confusion. Therefore, the rumors circulating in recent days that Japanese troops were taking action in Zhabei were entirely due to this misunderstanding. At the same time, it is possible that some troublemakers deliberately created alarm or spread rumors to confuse people.

Yesterday Japanese Troops Visit Again Caused a False Alarm

Since our side took over District D, the Japanese Naval Headquarters has repeatedly requested the Fifth District Public Security Bureau to visit the Zhabei area. At that time, the Fifth District refused and did not allow it. Later, a staff officer was sent to the Takeover Committee to make a request, and it was agreed that visits to Zhabei would be allowed on the 28th and 29th. Therefore, on the morning of the 28th, the Fifth District Public Security Bureau sent a motorized bicycle team to guide them to the Dongbaoxing Road, Baoxing Road, and Hongjiang Road areas to avoid confusion and panic among residents. At around 10:00 AM yesterday, the Fifth District Public Security Bureau branch sent a police team to guide them to the District D area for a visit. The Japanese troops visiting Zhabei on these two days were completely unarmed, with about 80 people traveling in cars. However, the residents of Zhabei, still jittery, inevitably became alarmed when they saw this. Some even planned to relocate. At the same time, a group of ignorant people spread rumors in various directions, causing the city to become alarmed, like a tiger in the market and a snake in a cup. In fact, the Japanese troops only patrolled in cars with public security bureau police officers before leaving. The residents immediately felt relieved.

Traitors Disturbing Public Security, Police Force Sufficient to Maintain Order

A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency made a special trip to the municipal government yesterday to inquire about the truth of the matter. A responsible official replied that a detailed investigation had been conducted and there was no factual basis. It was found that the rumors were entirely created by traitors and troublemakers. The police security team stationed in Zhabei by the municipal government has sufficient strength and is more than capable of maintaining the security of the area.

Japanese Troops Withdrew from the Public University Yarn Factory in Zhabei Yesterday Morning

Moved to the Dakang Yarn Factory

Without Notifying Our Side

Riri News Agency said that when our committee member Yu Hongjun of the Joint Committee repeatedly negotiated with Japanese committee member Okazaki regarding the exact date of withdrawal of Japanese troops from the Yinxiang Township Pingliang Road Public University Yarn Factory and the Huxi Toyota Yarn Factory, Okazaki repeatedly said that the troops stationed in the two factories were there before the January 28th Incident. Our Yu replied that the two factories were located in the Chinese concession and should be protected by our police force and could not be permanently stationed there, causing confusion among the people. Later, Okazaki, because our reasons were sufficient, agreed that the troops in District D would withdraw, and the troops in the two factories would continue to withdraw. Since the withdrawal of Japanese troops from District D on the 17th of this month, there has been no indication from the Japanese side regarding the exact date of withdrawal of Japanese troops from the two factories. However, yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, the Japanese side suddenly withdrew a platoon of more than 30 soldiers from the Second Battalion of the Japanese Naval Landing Force stationed at the Pingliang Road Public University Yarn Factory and moved them to the Dakang Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road. According to an investigation by a Riri News Agency reporter, although the matter was true, the Japanese side did not notify our side yesterday.

No Meeting at the Song Residence Yesterday

Song Suffered from Diarrhea and Temporarily Did Not See Guests

Central News Agency said that Finance Minister Song Ziwen, due to the need to further liaise with various parties in Shanghai regarding the issue of blockading the Northeast customs and reforming the conversion of silver to yuan, came to Shanghai by plane from Beijing the day before yesterday. After arriving in Shanghai, Song felt unwell and immediately asked British doctor McLeish to treat him. A reporter from the Central News Agency learned of Song's condition and other news and reported it as follows:

Song's Condition According to Guo Dehua, secretary of the Ministry of Finance, after visiting Song's residence, told a Central News Agency reporter that Song was planning finances and traveling between Beijing, Shanghai, Pinghan, and unavoidable fatigue. In addition, the weather has been extremely hot recently, and air travel is prone to both coolness and heat. Therefore, Song felt unwell immediately after arriving in Shanghai. Song is currently suffering from diarrhea and has also lost weight. This morning (i.e., yesterday morning), he again asked British doctor McLeish to treat him. It is said that he accidentally caught a cold and was instructed to rest, and he would fully recover in one or two days.

No Meeting Yesterday Song followed the doctor's instructions, closed the door, and declined guests. Therefore, those who went to visit yesterday were turned away. However, Tax Officer Westerner Guo Peng, Jianghai Customs Supervisor Tang Hai'an, and Secretary of the Ministry of Finance Guo Dehua were summoned by Song yesterday morning and spoke for a short time before leaving. Therefore, there was no meeting at the Song residence yesterday.

Recovering and Leaving Shanghai According to reporters, Song was originally scheduled to fly back to Beijing by the original plane last night, but because his diarrhea had not fully recovered, the doctor instructed him not to fly. Therefore, Song decided to stay in Shanghai temporarily and return to Beijing after he had fully recovered. Song's disciple Ziliang took a boat to Mount Lu last night, and it is said that Song also plans to go to Mount Lu after he recovers. Song's wife, Zhang Lehua, is currently vacationing in Mount Lu.

Blocking Customs Needs Further Consideration

Our agency's reporter received news yesterday from sources close to the Song family that Song's primary objective during this visit remains the blockade of the Northeast customs, with military expenditure reduction being secondary. It is rumored that the blockade of the Northeast customs will be implemented on August 1st. However, this may not be so rapid, as customs duties are not comparable to postal services. In the future, if Northeast goods are exported from Dalian and shipped to China by sea, how can their origin as products of the puppet state be proven? Tianjin customs is restricted by treaties and is not a central hub for goods entering North China from the Eastern Provinces. Therefore, the central government faces significant difficulties in this matter. In addition to Song, those participating in the discussion of this issue naturally include Zhang Fuyun, the Director-General of Customs; Meilleur, the Inspector General of Customs; Zhang Shouyong, an advisor; and foreign advisors from the Ministry of Finance. These individuals have consistently refrained from divulging any information regarding the Northeast customs issue, indicating the gravity of the matter. They fear that the blockade order, when issued, will exist in name only and lack substance, merely exposing their own weaknesses. Consequently, the central government is cautiously approaching this matter and will not issue a blockade order until fully confident. With only two days left until August 1st, if it is implemented as scheduled, there must be an order from the customs authorities today. As this concerns all parties, the absence of such news suggests that there are difficulties and ongoing discussions, making a swift implementation on the first day unlikely.

Japanese Oppose Our Double Taxation

Representation by the Japanese Consul

Tashiro's Opinion

According to the Shih Wen News Agency, the Shanghai Customs authorities plan to levy full import and export taxes on goods shipped from Shanghai to the Northeast starting August 1st, in accordance with the new regulations. In response to this issue, the Japanese Affairs Committee specially appointed Administrative Committee Chairman Yasui yesterday to appeal to the Japanese Consul and to negotiate countermeasures. Simultaneously, Major General Tashiro, newly transferred from Tokyo to Shanghai as the military attache of the Japanese Consulate General, convened meetings with military officers stationed in Shanghai, including Kita, Ogine, Nemoto, and Tanaka, at the Japanese Club for several consecutive days to coordinate all matters.

The Japanese Consul stated that Yasui, the acting chairman of the Japanese Affairs Committee, visited the Japanese Consulate General yesterday afternoon around 1:00 PM, representing all Japanese merchants, to appeal to Murai regarding the decision by the Chinese Customs to levy full import and export taxes on goods shipped to the Northeast starting August 1st. Murai stated that regarding the issue of Shanghai Customs levying double taxes on goods shipped to the Northeast starting next month, which concerns the entire trade with China, the government has decided to lodge a strong protest when the Chinese Customs begins collecting the double taxes on August 1st. He stated that he had no authority to negotiate with the Chinese government. However, in his opinion, the Chinese government is indeed violating the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce and Navigation. The reason given by the Chinese government for levying double taxes on goods shipped to the Northeast is the puppet state of Manchuria's takeover of the Dalian Customs. However, the puppet state's takeover of the Northeast customs was entirely voluntary. All responsibilities should be borne by the puppet state of Manchuria. It is incomprehensible that the Chinese government is not negotiating with the responsible country but is resorting to double taxation, causing undue suffering to our merchants. He stated that he had repeatedly telegraphed the government, urging them to negotiate with the Chinese government as soon as possible. He further stated that the government's reply had arrived in Shanghai, stating that if the Chinese Customs indeed implements this taxation on August 1st, it will lodge a strong protest on the same day. Therefore, he could confidently assure the overseas residents (referring to Yasui) not to panic.

Tashiro's Opinion Major General Tashiro, the military staff officer dispatched by the Japanese during the Shanghai War, has been newly appointed as the military attache of the Consulate General in Shanghai and is deeply concerned with the issues of China's double taxation in the Northeast and countermeasures against the boycott of Japanese goods. Yesterday and today, Major General Tashiro also convened important meetings with military officers stationed in Shanghai, including Kita, Ogine, Nemoto, and Tanaka, at the Japanese Club. During the two-day meeting, there was a detailed discussion regarding the issue of the Chinese Customs levying double taxes on goods shipped to the Northeast and countermeasures against anti-Japanese sentiment. According to the Shih Wen News Agency's reporter, Major General Tashiro expressed his opinion on the issue of China's double taxation during yesterday's meeting, stating that since the Shanghai War, the Japanese merchants in Shanghai have been greatly affected. At that time, even though he was a dispatched military staff officer, he could not protect them to continue their business. After the end of the war, the Japanese merchants tried their best to restore their former state and have been working hard on reorganization until now. Fortunately, they have recovered slightly. However, the Chinese government, under the pretext of the puppet state of Manchuria taking over the Dalian Customs, is implementing import and export taxes on goods shipped to the Northeast. This action by the Chinese government is solely directed against Japan. However, the puppet state of Manchuria and Japan can be said to have no relationship, so why should it take the blame for others? Moreover, this matter is of great loss to our trade with the Northeast. Now, the Shanghai Customs is said to be starting the levy on the first day of next month, so this matter seems to have become a reality. The only way to deal with it at present is to protect it by military force, and there is no other way. Because the transportation of goods into the Northeast cannot bypass any Chinese customs and reach it directly. He believes that this policy of military protection of freight should be implemented simultaneously from the day the Chinese Customs begins to levy double taxes. He is also very willing to work hard to promote this matter to relieve the suffering of our merchants.

Lin Shi Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Discussing Measures to Deal with the Northeastern Postal Blockade with Huang Naishu The Central News Agency reports that Lin Shi, the Director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Transportation, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing at around 8:00 AM yesterday. Huang Naishu, the Director-General of Posts, and others welcomed him at the North Station. After getting off the train, Lin immediately accompanied Director Huang back to his residence on Rue du Père Froc to rest briefly and then went to the Postal Bureau on North Sichuan Road to discuss the aftermath of the postal blockade in the Northeast. He only returned to his residence at noon. At 5:00 PM, he went to the United Press to attend the Postal Economic System Research Committee. The reporter met Lin at the North Station yesterday and inquired about various postal issues, to which he replied item by item as follows: (Q) Director Lin, what is the purpose of your visit to Shanghai this time? (A) I am here to discuss the aftermath of the postal blockade in the Northeast with Director Huang Naishu and to attend the Postal Economic System Research Committee. (Q) How will we deal with the illegal temporary post offices set up by Japanese residents in Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places? (A) The Postal Bureau is currently investigating the truth of this matter. If it damages our sovereignty, the government will have to negotiate seriously. (Q) Is it illegal for Japanese residents in Shanghai to transport Northeastern mail by Dalian steamers? (A) The Postal Bureau has dispatched personnel to investigate this matter. A decision will be made on whether it is illegal after the truth is obtained, and then countermeasures will be considered. (Q) How will we deal with the Japanese side affixing Japanese stamps to mail from the puppet state to various countries and illegally arresting our withdrawn postal employees? (A) This is not only an act of infringement but also undermines the integrity of our country's administrative sovereignty. The diplomatic authorities must lodge a protest. (Q) Is it true that Horiuchi, the secretary of the Japanese Embassy, went to Nanjing to mediate the postal blockade in the Northeast? (A) I have not met Horiuchi, nor have I heard of this matter. (Q) Since the postal blockade in the Northeast, mail to Europe has been rerouted by sea, which is many days slower than by land. How will the Ministry of Transportation remedy this? (A) The Ministry of Transportation is actively pursuing Euro-Asia aviation to make up for this deficiency. (Q) When will Director Lin return to Nanjing? (A) I will stay in Shanghai for about two days before returning to Nanjing. According to staff members of the Postal Bureau, the local office received Northeastern mail sent from Dalian yesterday. All of these mails had sufficient Chinese stamps affixed and were sent before the blockade. No traitorous stamps were found in the delivered mails. If any are found in the future, they will be immediately detained. It is still under consideration whether to detain mails with sufficient Chinese stamps affixed that are sent from the Northeast in the future. As for the Japanese side preventing Northeastern postal employees from entering the customs, after Ba Lide, the Postal Director of the Liaoning District, lodged a strong protest, the Japanese side, realizing their lack of justification, verbally agreed to issue entry permits and promised to provide protection along the way. Ba has reported the previous situation to the General Post Office. As of yesterday, a total of 450 Northeastern postal employees have requested to receive entry permits. These employees will be able to enter the customs within a few days and report to nearby post offices for assignment.

Huge Losses in the Northeast Zhu Menghou, the Director of the General Affairs Department of the Postal Bureau, told our agency's reporter yesterday that the real estate, such as postal buildings, etc., in the Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang districts, is estimated at more than 2 million yuan. This time, it was seized by the puppet state at the instigation of the Japanese. In addition, the movable property is not included in the total, and the total number is not yet accurately investigated. The annual surplus of more than 2 million yuan will also become a bubble.

Postal Workers Prepare to Enter Customs The General Post Office received a telegram yesterday from Ba Lide, the Director of the Liaoning District Postal Administration, reporting on the entry of postal personnel into the customs. After Ba's repeated negotiations with the other party, they have agreed not to obstruct them any longer and have agreed to issue entry permits. Another report stated that there are more than 450 postal workers concentrated in Shenyang waiting for permits to enter the customs.

Puppet Postal Items Arrive Today After the puppet state forcibly seized our Northeast postal service, the first batch of mail sent from Harbin, Siberia, and other places in the three northeastern provinces to Shanghai was telegraphed to Shanghai yesterday. It has been shipped by the Dalian Fengtian Maru and is expected to arrive in Shanghai at 4:30 PM today. The Japanese temporary post office at the Japanese Club has assigned Japanese personnel to pick it up at the dock at that time and then hire coolies to distribute it to various places in this city.

The Fragrance Industry Strike Expands

Party and Government Agencies Sent Personnel Yesterday to Investigate Thoroughly

After the fragrance industry workers in this city went on strike to demand better treatment, the strike completely affected Pudong and the concessions yesterday. Party and government agencies sent personnel to conduct a thorough investigation. The details are as follows:

The Social Affairs Bureau Replies to the Fragrance Industry Trade Union The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, considering that all industries are depressed and have not yet recovered after the war, and in accordance with the municipal government's announcement, has advised both labor and management to work together to overcome difficulties. It has issued an order to the union, stating that the request to convene the capital side to amend the labor-capital conditions and increase wages has been noted, and it has been determined that the original energy has not yet recovered after the war, so the request should be postponed. This approval is temporarily stored.

The Strike Expands After the fragrance industry workers in the Nanshi Zhabei area spontaneously went on strike the day before yesterday, the workers in various stores in the Pudong Concession also joined, acting in unison to urge the capital side to wake up. The number of participating stores is 105, with more than 450 workers. However, the employees of the store's front offices, as well as more than 220 people, still worked as usual yesterday.

Party and Government Investigation The Social Affairs Bureau, on account of the spontaneous strike by the fragrance industry workers, dispatched Zhu Guilin, together with Li Weitai of the Municipal Party Department, to rush to investigate the truth in order to verify the matter. The union yesterday submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department, requesting a quick mediation to eliminate disputes. According to the owner of Weishan Zhai, the fragrance industry has been naturally eliminated in recent times, and business has plummeted. They have all reduced their business scope, resulting in a gradual increase in the number of unemployed. They hope that the labor side will embrace a spirit of cooperation, resume work first, and then negotiate a solution, otherwise, they can only let it take its natural course.

Original Conditions Listed The original text of the conditions proposed by the union is listed below: (1) The capital side recognizes the union's right to represent all workers; (2) All employee wages, regardless of apprenticeship or the size of the wages, shall be increased by 40% from the original wages, and the monthly regulations for workers and students shall be increased to 1.4 yuan per month; (3) If the union has a formal meeting and national memorial days, all holidays announced by the Party and government agencies shall be given in accordance with the regulations, and wages shall be paid as usual. The capital side shall not deliberately make things difficult; (4) The working hours for employees shall be from 8:00 AM to 5:00 PM, but during the seventh and a half to eighth and a half months of the lunar calendar and the twelfth month of the lunar calendar, when night work is allowed, the time shall be from 6:30 PM to 10:00 PM. Employees shall apply for work seven days a month. The packaging department shall stop work on the first and fifteenth days of each lunar month, and wages shall be paid as usual; (5) The capital side shall not arbitrarily dismiss employees. If there is illegal behavior, report to the union, and those who decide to dismiss must be supplemented by unemployed personnel who have passed the worker's review; (6) Workers who ask for leave for weddings, funerals, and special events shall not have their wages deducted; (7) The capital side shall not be hostile to workers who are elected as union directors and supervisors; (8) If a worker is sick, the capital side shall bear the medical expenses, and wages shall be paid as usual, up to a maximum of two months; (9) The minimum monthly allowance for employees after graduation shall be 6 yuan, and one apprentice may be received within three years; (10) If the opinions of the workers on both sides disagree and they withdraw, the capital side shall bear one month's wages for one year; (11) The workers' annual fees, section regulations, and church dishes shall all be increased by 40%; (12) All violations of the above items 3, 5, 6, and 8 shall be punished; (13) These conditions shall be implemented after both parties sign and are approved by the Party and government agencies.

The Extra-Settlement Road Construction Case Remains Undecided

Increased Tuition Fees at Chinese Public Schools

The Shanghai Municipal Council Board of Directors convened its last meeting before the summer break at 4:30 PM yesterday. Because the meetings must be suspended several times from next week until they are convened again in September, the details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

Extra-Settlement Road Construction Issue Regarding the extra-settlement road construction issue, the Municipal Council has recently made some revisions to the original draft agreement. Yu Hongjun, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, and Fessenden, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, have conducted several rounds of consultations. The original text of the content will be issued today but has not been announced.

Page 14

Increased Tuition Fees for Chinese Schools It was also discussed to increase tuition fees for Chinese schools under the jurisdiction of the bureau. According to the original plan of the Municipal Council, starting from the next semester of this year, the tuition fees for the secondary school part will be increased from 40 yuan to 48 yuan, and the primary school part will be increased by 3 yuan. After the Chinese Directors objected, it was decided at yesterday's meeting to increase it by 4 yuan in the next month of this year and another 4 yuan next year. The primary school part will not be increased for the time being.

Settlement Amnesty Incident Recent statistics show that there are more than 7,000 accumulated prisoners in the Huade Road Prison in the Public Concession. Since the National Government issued the amnesty decree, about 2,000 people have been pardoned in the concession. The Municipal Council believes that the release of a large number of pardoned prisoners may hinder the security of the concession. It was also proposed for discussion at the last meeting. At yesterday's meeting, the Director-General slightly communicated with the Chinese Directors, hoping that after the release of a large number of pardoned prisoners, the public groups and hometown associations in the concession could provide the bureau with assistance in separately repatriating or providing funds for them to make a living. All the Chinese Directors present agreed. The meeting adjourned at 5:15 PM.

The Northwest Reclamation Corps Will Depart for Suiyuan on August 1st

Mayor Wu Presents Travel Expenses and a Written Inscription

Samsung Cotton Iron Factory Specially Donates Uniforms

The Frontier Society Hosted a Farewell Dinner Yesterday

Scheduled to Host Reporters This Afternoon

The Northwest is an important area for our country's national defense and industrial development. Reclamation in the Northwest is related to the safety and security of our country's foundation and the happiness and suffering of people's livelihoods. Yan Ziduan and others, aware of this, have organized the Northwest Reclamation Corps, which is scheduled to depart for Suiyuan on August 1st to conduct investigations. Yesterday, Huang Jingwan, a representative of the Chinese Frontier Society, specially hosted a farewell dinner for the departing personnel at the Yunji Sichuan Restaurant on Sanma Road. Mayor Wu Tiecheng also presented travel expenses and the four characters "Jueyu Shuguang" (Dawn in a Remote Region). In addition, the Samsung Cotton Iron Factory also specially made and donated uniforms to the departing personnel. The corps is scheduled to host the local press at the Qingnianhui Building on Baxianqiao today at noon. The establishment process of the corps, etc., is summarized as follows:

Establishment Process According to the corps leader Yan Ziduan, speaking to our agency's reporter about the motivation and establishment process of the Northwest Reclamation Corps, the corps was established in July last year. At the National Vocational Education Discussion Conference, there was a proposal to develop the frontier to find a way out for young people. An implementation outline was drafted and submitted for discussion. At that time, there were different opinions on developing the frontier of the province and developing the Northeast. After I explained that the Northeast already has 30 million people, allowing them to develop on their own, and that it can be postponed for the time being, although there are wastelands in various provinces waiting to be reclaimed, it is not related to the overall situation. Only the Northwest is empty and is also the passageway for Euro-Asia transportation. If we do not plan for it now, I am afraid that it will not be ours in the future. Moreover, the progress of a country should be based on balanced development as a principle, and a comprehensive plan is especially necessary to avoid abuses. As a result, the atmosphere of the entire venue became tense, and the outline was unanimously passed. If we can get the government's promotion and capitalists' participation, it will not be difficult to compete with foreign business groups such as the South Manchuria Railway Company and exclude them. In the middle, it was suspended for several months due to disaster relief and anti-Japanese resistance, and it was postponed again and again until the preparatory committee was established in October last year. Then the plan was finalized, the charter was properly drafted, and it was not until today that it was able to depart for investigation. This is the general situation of the motivation for the organization of this corps and the process after its establishment.

Departing Personnel On August 1st, the departing personnel include Ms. Wen Duanshen (a graduate of the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University), Corps Leader Yan Ziduan, Corps Members Cai Songmin, Lin Weiru, Fang Lifang, Zhou Xuede, Zhu Wenjian, Zhang Jianchu, Xiao Tianhen, Feng Yikang, Li Ji'an, Chen Peisheng, Hu Biaoyi, and Yan Hannan, a total of 14 people.

Hosting Reporters The corps specially issued invitations yesterday, inviting reporters from various newspapers and news agencies to the Qingnianhui Building on Baxianqiao to report on the departure investigation and future plans.

Departure Declaration As the European War comes to an end, the world is showing active progress. The center of the world has shifted from the Mediterranean and Atlantic Oceans to the Pacific Ocean, and the scope is expanding. Therefore, the European War broke out because of the Balkan issue and ended with the United States joining. The real world war in the future may be triggered by the China issue. Our pioneer and visionary Sun Yat-sen foresaw this and wanted to use the International Development of China's Industrial Plan to eliminate disasters before they take shape and to save the overall situation of the world. Unfortunately, it was not implemented, and Mr. Sun died with his ambition unfulfilled. The industrial plan lists the Northwest Grand Railway first, and its importance is evident. The martyr Zhu Zhixin has also spoken with emotion. The comrades of this corps once suggested to the government that a Central Engineering Bureau be organized to complete this railway as its own responsibility, but it was not adopted. In a situation of helplessness, the Northwest Reclamation Corps was initiated. Knowing that a mayfly is not enough to shake a mountain and that a lone army is setting in the sun, we secretly want to imitate Lu Yang's waving of his halberd. Now, Outer Mongolia is independent, Tibetan bandits are pressing in, and natural disasters and man-made disasters are intensifying each other. The Northeast is also hearing about the Japanese army invading. The people of the country fear the imminent demise and do not know what plan to come up with. Moreover, the trouble in the world lies in what ordinary people do not realize. The Northeast must have today, or it will be even worse than today. The reason lies in the decades ago, due to the people of the country not knowing how to cherish it. Comparing the Northeast to the Northwest is like comparing the great Tokyo earthquake in Japan to the Pingliang earthquake in Gansu. The people of the country only know the intensity of the earthquake in Japan, but they do not know that the earthquake in Gansu far exceeds it. The dangerous situation in the Northeast is already fully known to the people of the country. The dangerous situation in the Northwest is ten or a hundred times that of the Northeast, and the people of the country still do not know it. The wealth of the Northeast has been made known to the world because of Tanaka's active policy. It is not known that the treasures of the Northwest are beyond the dreams of the people of the country. Some say, "With such a small private group, to carry out such a huge global undertaking, isn't it absurd?" I will answer, "No." Doesn't the guest observe the South Manchuria Railway and the East India Company? Under the resistance and jealousy of foreigners, they can still flourish and grow, and destroy human countries without knowing it. Therefore, although this corps is small, it has the support of the government above and the support of the people of the country below. If we say that it will be ineffective, I do not believe it. However, there is one word that I cannot but attach to this, that the people of the country are usually drunk and confused, and they are unwilling to slightly divide their minds and resources on the fundamental national plan to jointly support it. Once disaster strikes and the country is in danger, they are so busy and exhausted that they have to reluctantly break their stingy bags to make the final patch, and it is already too late. This invisibly wears down social vitality and is extremely regrettable. It is also like the people of the country all know that construction is the key plan, but they are unwilling to pool their efforts to achieve it. By the time social order is not guaranteed, before the knives and cauldrons, raising military expenses is a painful and difficult task, and they can do it on the spot, squandering huge sums of money in a place where nothing exists. Repeating the cycle, it will inevitably lead to national destruction and species extinction. How different is it from a person not knowing hygiene, working hard for a day, and diseases arising, but willingly suffering the pain of surgery and medication, and not stopping until the vitality is greatly damaged? This kind of mentality, if the strings are not changed, the national situation will never be saved. My colleagues are alarmed by the imminent disaster and struggle in the midst of difficulties. We have already organized and established this corps and strive to be the vanguard of the people of the country. The personal livelihood problem is solved by it, and the strengthening of national defense and the development of the frontier will benefit both the public and the private sectors. It is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep is lost, and to collect the mulberry elm in the east. This declaration is hereby made.

Japanese Persisting Vigorously

The Yangtze River Japanese steamers have been suspended for a long time. The various shipping companies are trying to resume operations, and the Japanese government has allocated funds to subsidize them. It was originally scheduled to be implemented on August 1st, but due to the "Blood Souls Assassination Squad" incident in Shanghai warning treacherous merchants, it had to be temporarily postponed and other countermeasures sought. The details are recorded below:

Failure to Resume: The Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (Japanese Shipping Company) currently operating on the Yangtze River route has three vessels on the southern route: Nanyo Maru, Hoyo Maru, and Joyo Maru; two vessels on the northern route: Kazan Maru and Tozan Maru; and two vessels on the southern route: Rozan Maru and Sozan Maru. All have been suspended due to the impact of the boycott. The Shanghai manager, Mr. Yoneri, had planned to resume operations on August 1st. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency recently interviewed a senior official of the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, who stated that the Japanese merchants' plan to restore shipping is being kept strictly secret. However, due to the ongoing and intense Chinese boycott of Japanese goods, each time a Japanese steamer sails, it is loaded with transshipped Japanese goods. Chinese goods are nowhere to be seen, and there are very few Chinese passengers. In addition, the recent actions of the "Blood Souls Assassination Squad" have dealt a major blow. It is reported that the planned resumption on August 1st has now been postponed, but the reporter has learned that the Japanese are proceeding very vigorously.

Current Routes: The Dalian Steamship Company mainly operates on the northern route, currently operating only the Hoten Maru, Dairen Maru, and Tientsin Maru. The Osaka Shosen Kaisha mainly operates on foreign and northern routes. The foreign routes, such as those to Europe, South America, Africa, and New Zealand, are still operating as usual. Only the northern routes, such as those served by the Seikyo Maru, Choshu Maru, and Fukien Maru, are operating. The Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK Line) is dedicated to foreign routes, such as those to Hong Kong, Bombay, Europe, New York, Seattle, and San Francisco, all of which are operating as usual. Although the above three companies have been subjected to the Chinese boycott movement, they have not been greatly affected.

Chinese Consulates Abroad Required to Certify Goods - Japanese Business Groups Object

Shi Wen News Agency reports: Japanese business groups in Shanghai, including the Shanghai Japanese Business Federation, the Cotton Textile Industry Association, and the Chamber of Commerce, object to the Chinese government's planned implementation on September 1st of a policy requiring Chinese consular certification of goods. All goods valued at over 200 yuan that are to be transported into the Chinese mainland must first be certified by the Chinese consul in the place of origin and a fee of 1.05 customs gold units (approximately 8 Japanese yen) collected. The aforementioned Japanese business groups believe that most Japanese merchants in Shanghai operate on a small scale, and shipments of goods worth two or three hundred yuan to Shanghai are common. They are determined not to pay the consular certification fee in addition to the import tax. Therefore, they held an emergency meeting at the Japanese Residents' Association last night to discuss countermeasures. As a result, it was resolved that the above-listed groups would send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in the name of their organizations, requesting that it negotiate with the Chinese government to cancel this new measure. The telegram was sent out at 8:00 PM last night. The groups will reconvene to discuss further measures once they receive a reply from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Shanghai Maritime Circles Again Fight to Recover Foreign Pilotage Rights

Regarding the recovery of pilotage rights, the Shanghai maritime community exerted all its efforts to fight for it last year. During the Shanghai Battle this year, enemy ships entered and exited Wusong, transporting troops and equipment, all guided by members of the foreign pilotage association, aiding the enemy and endangering national defense. If pilotage rights had been recovered earlier, the Japanese troops would have had no way to enter the country during the January 28th Incident, let alone penetrate Liuhe to cut off our reinforcements. The outcome is uncertain. Therefore, it is felt that striving for recovery is an urgent task. The Shanghai Merchant Marine Masters Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Maritime Affairs Bureau, requesting that it be forwarded to the ministry, to vigorously fight for the recovery of maritime administration and pilotage rights, with March 5th of next year being the date of expiration of the foreign pilots' permits. The original text states: "We petition that the pilotage at the mouth of the Yangtze River and the coastal port administration are controlled by foreigners, aiding the enemy and endangering the country, which has been seen repeatedly. We request that this be forwarded to the ministry to vigorously fight for recovery, replace them with Chinese, to eliminate great harm and secure national defense. We have investigated the origin of the foreign pilots at the mouth of the Yangtze River. It is neither related to any treaty nor based on any legal position. It is simply an act of aggression against our country by imperialists in the past, forming a non-descript organization. Since the establishment of this organization, for six or seventy years, they have relied on their special power to occupy territory, monopolize traffic, and meticulously plan to oppose the government and undermine sovereignty at any time and in any place. Whenever there is war, these foreign pilots openly lead foreign warships into ports, attacking and aiding the enemy. This has been seen repeatedly. In the distant past, during the Sino-French War of the Qing Dynasty, the French warships that attacked the Min River and defeated our navy were led by an American pilot holding a customs license. The facts of losing the army and humiliating the country are recorded in Moore's public law, which scholars of public law in various countries have described as a strange tale. More recently, during the January 28th Incident, all enemy warships transporting troops and equipment, entering and exiting ports, were piloted by members of the foreign pilotage association, helping to attack our Shanghai, reflecting and echoing each other, known throughout the country. Other places in the Yangtze River were able to penetrate deeply, launching flanking attacks on the 19th Route Army, thanks to them. Therefore, for decades, the harm caused by foreign pilots has been great, endangering national defense. The facts are clear and not an exaggeration on our part. In July of last year, the Maritime Pilot Training Institute and the Hydrographic Survey Bureau received an order from the ministry, stating that the Executive Yuan had telegraphed the customs, ordering the suspension of the issuance of new permits to foreign pilots from July 1st of that year. Unexpectedly, after investigation, the Inspector General of Customs single-mindedly favored and protected foreign pilots, ignoring the government's orders and continuing to issue permits. According to our country's pilotage examination regulations, which were promulgated and implemented on March 5th of the 20th year, foreign pilots would not be allowed to serve after March 5th of next year. Our country originally planned to hold this examination last year, jointly organized by the Ministries of Finance, Communications, and Navy, but it was quickly shelved and has not been realized. The key to this lies in the secret machinations of these foreigners, whose influence is all-pervasive, a lamentable situation. Furthermore, regarding the suspension of the issuance of new permits, the Executive Yuan had issued a clear order, but the Inspector General of Customs openly resisted and violated it, yet all parties turned a blind eye, allowing it to continue to this point. What else can be said? The foreign pilotage association has ulterior motives, which did not begin today. Examining their behavior, they are no less than an organized espionage group. The credo of the association is to keep the secret conditions of the port channels as the primary task. Other shipping regulations and service records are not important. Proof of this can be seen in the troubles caused by the association members since July 1st of last year. The most obvious examples are the changes to the Indian ship in November and the collision of the Buddan steamer with the dock on July 6th of this month. The responsibility of the members is invariably covered up. The inside story is that there are secrets that cannot be revealed, and they dare not take overly aggressive actions. In short, the existence of this association is a hidden danger to our country, posing a great danger to national defense and military affairs. What has been stated above is mostly past fact. Your bureau is the only competent maritime administration agency of the government in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. It seems that you cannot feign ignorance and allow the foreign pilots and customs officials to collude with each other to plot against us. You should consider the overall situation, forward a request to the ministry, make a firm decision, eliminate concerns, recover foreign pilotage in accordance with the time limit stipulated in the examination regulations, replace them with Chinese, and vigorously fight for the Ministry of Finance to order the customs to hand over coastal port administration to the Maritime Affairs Bureau for management. Even if things do not go as desired, you may as well disclose all the details and make them public opinion. Even if it fails, it can still be declared innocent to the people and leave a good name to posterity. Compared with those who procrastinate and are perfunctory, harming themselves and the country, the magnitude of the gains and losses is almost incalculable. Today, the world is in decline and people are lost. Our association, as a technical group earning a living through labor, is fortunate to be living in this world. Lacking the ability to seek favors, we do not avoid taboos, and speak frankly. Whether it is appropriate or not, we hope you will review and approve it." This document was delivered yesterday.

International Trade Association Suggests Imported Foreign Goods Must Be Labeled with Origin

Emergency Plan for Import Surplus Country

Guo Bingwen, Chairman of the International Trade Association, yesterday submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry, stating: "We submit a petition to the Ministry of Finance to clearly stipulate rules that imported foreign goods should be labeled with the name of the country of origin in clear characters on the conspicuous place of the goods' packaging and boxes. We respectfully request adoption and implementation. It is our understanding that China's industrial and commercial sectors are still immature, and the output of domestic goods is insufficient to meet demand. It is necessary to import and sell essential foreign goods to meet domestic needs. Exchange of goods is a natural matter. However, imported goods vary in quality, and their costs vary due to the nationality and status of the country of origin. It is a loss to the national economy to import more than export, and it is necessary for people's livelihood to seek economy by choosing the superior and selecting the excellent. For example, if the goods of country A have a lower cost, lower quality, and easier transportation, but in order to obtain a better price, they imitate the higher quality and more expensive goods of country B at the time of import, or even change their appearance and re-enter from other countries, it will inevitably lead to fish eyes mixed with pearls, increasing the burden on buyers, and causing double losses to the national economy and people's livelihood. The great loss is unbearable. Article 304 of the US tariff law clearly stipulates that imported goods must have a mark of origin, otherwise there will be additional taxes, no delivery, and penalty rules. The United States is an exporting country, and it severely cracks down on foreign goods entering the country. Last year, China's import surplus reached 500 million yuan. How can we continue to ignore this? The association, at its fifth board meeting, resolved to petition the ministry to suggest that the Ministry of Finance establish specific rules that imported foreign goods should be labeled with the name of the country of origin in clear characters on the conspicuous place of the goods' packaging and boxes, otherwise, higher taxes will be levied, or delivery will be prohibited. Those who cheat and deceive will be severely fined and strictly enforced by customs, hoping to slightly benefit the national economy and people's livelihood, and also protect international commercial ethics. Whether it is appropriate or not, we have prepared a document and translated the full text of Article 304 of the US tariff law, requesting adoption and implementation, and requesting instructions to follow."

Minutes of the Meeting of the Money Trade Association

The Shanghai Money Trade Association held a newspaper committee meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than ten people attended, chaired by Qin Runqing. There was a long discussion on issues such as the Money Trade Joint Reserve and the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan. Regarding the Reserve, it was decided in principle that it should not engage in business activities with external parties. All exchange-drawing peers are members of the Reserve's funding foundation. Yuan-character shops among the small peers (small peers are those who do not engage in exchange-drawing, and are divided into Yuan, Heng, Li, etc.) can also join as ordinary members. The Reserve's charter was also revised once and will be submitted for further discussion at the meeting on August 2nd.

Huang Boqiao and Shen Yi Departed for Beijing Last Night

Participating in the Two-Roads Recovery Construction Conference

The Municipal Government previously planned to recover the Songhu Railway and return it to municipal management, and consulted the Ministry of Railways. The director of the Public Works Bureau, Huang Boqiao, and the director of the Engineering Bureau, Shen Yi, were sent to Beijing yesterday to participate in the Two-Roads Recovery Construction Conference, where this matter will be discussed in detail. According to Ding Xingheng, Secretary of the Bureau, who spoke to the East China News Agency yesterday, the Songhu Railway is an auxiliary branch of the Jinghu Railway and was built with loans from Sino-British companies. Changes to the Building Permit Application Procedures for Wusong and Jiangwan

Engineering Bureau Sets Up Permit Issuance Offices in Both Locations

Since Wusong and Jiangwan districts were devastated by war, most of the houses and dwellings need to be rebuilt and repaired. In order to facilitate the people and meet the actual needs, the Municipal Engineering Bureau has been approved by the Municipal Government to set up permit issuance offices in Wusong Town and Jiangwan Town. At the same time, in order to rectify municipal administration, the permit application procedures for the two districts have been changed. Although projects that were previously exempt from permits must now obtain permits, no permit fees will be charged, as a gesture of consideration. The bureau's announcement is recorded below: Announcement regarding the 128 Incident, the houses and dwellings in the Wusong and Jiangwan districts were mostly destroyed by artillery fire. Now that the situation is gradually stabilizing, these destroyed houses all need to be rebuilt and repaired. In order to facilitate the people in the two districts and meet the actual needs, this bureau has been approved by the Municipal Government to set up permit issuance offices in Wusong Town and Jiangwan Town to handle the issuance of permits and the survey and guidance of all repairs. At the same time, the permit application procedures have been changed. All projects that were temporarily exempt from permits in the two districts will now be subject to the city's temporary building rules, that is, projects such as building single-story houses with less than ten rooms and repairing fences must apply for permits in accordance with the regulations before work can begin. However, no permit fees will be charged to alleviate the people's difficulties. In addition to renting a house on Kuizhao Road in Jiangwan Town to set up a permit issuance office, the Wusong Town permit issuance office will be temporarily located in the office of the municipal commissioner before a house is rented. Furthermore, the municipal commissioners of the two districts have been ordered to stop accepting reports on single-story houses from August 1st. This announcement is made for all to know.

National Anti-Drug Conference Scheduled

Date: August 29th to September 2nd

Location: Hangzhou YMCA

The National Anti-Drug Representative Conference convened by the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association was originally scheduled to be held in the spring, but was postponed due to the impact of the war. The Standing Committee of the Association recently resolved to hold it at the YMCA and the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters on the shores of West Lake in Hangzhou on the anniversary of the Treaty of Nanjing, August 29th of this year. The main purpose is to unify the national anti-drug movement, thoroughly eliminate the opium public sale, and urge the government to strictly enforce the ban on smoking. All representatives traveling to and from the conference have been agreed upon by the Association and the Railway Department to be given certificates entitling them to a 50% discount on train tickets on all lines directly under the Railway Department. Preparations in Hangzhou are being handled by the Zhejiang Provincial Anti-Drug Association at 6, Lane 3, Shangnongli, Qingnian Road. Preparations in Shanghai are being handled by the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association at 4 Hong Kong Road. It is reported that representatives from anti-drug groups in more than 40 places, including Beiping, Tianjin, Jinan, Chengdu, Lanzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Nanjing, Hankou, Ningbo, Singapore, Batavia, and Taiwan, have registered. More than 20 proposals have been received. It is reported that the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, and the Hangzhou Municipal Government all welcome the conference. The Municipal Government has also allocated a portion of the scenic area of Pinghu Qiuyue for the Association to establish a Lin Zexu Anti-Drug Memorial Hall. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Jianghuai People Organize the Jianghuai Water Conservancy Promotion Association

Yesterday's Declaration

Wu Yibai, Dai Shouyue, Lu Yuheng, Liang Yidong, Wang Muzun, Chen Chaobi, Shen Ziping, Zhao Junhao, Gu Jianwu, Zhu Difei, Chen Shaozeng, Yi Ziting, Xia Qifeng, Ding Jiansan, Ding Xiasheng, Ding Jimin, Ge Gongzhen and other Jianghuai natives in Shanghai initiated the Jianghuai Water Conservancy Promotion Association and issued a declaration yesterday, saying, "In recent years, floods have occurred frequently in Jiangbei, especially the disastrous disaster last year, which was unprecedented. More than 40 sections of the canal embankment collapsed, stretching over a thousand feet. The disaster area reached more than 200,000 square miles, the loss of property reached more than 400 million yuan, and the loss of life has not yet been accurately counted. Alas, it's a tragedy! We believe that the success or failure of Jianghuai water conservancy depends on the success of waterway management. However, waterway management and river diversion are closely related. The Huai River originates from Anhui and Henan, and converges in Anhui and Jiangsu. It flows eastward through Hongze Lake, passes through Zhangfu River to Matou Town, and enters the canal southward. It exits Sanhe Dam, passes through Gaoyou, Shaobo, and other lakes, and also enters the canal. Therefore, the Huai River uses the canal as its tail to divide and enter the rivers and seas. If you want to manage the canal, you must first divert the Huai River. This is an unchanging truth and an inevitable trend. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, Mr. Zhang Ji of Nantong published the Jianghuai Water Conservancy Plan, which determined the cost of diverting the Huai River and managing the canal to be 80 million yuan, but it was not implemented due to lack of funds. Now, experts in water conservancy at home and abroad have different opinions. The proposal for diverting the Huai River, entering the river or entering the sea, has not yet been decided. Although diverting the Huai River is indeed a fundamental solution, the project is huge and cannot be done in a short period of time. Managing the canal is a temporary solution, but thinking about it as a second best is also a crucial step. According to the records, in the third year of the Republic of China, the Jiangsu provincial authorities planned to develop Jianghuai water conservancy and convened Jianghuai gentry to discuss the construction of the inner canal project. It was initially assumed that the cost would be 1 million yuan, with 600,000 yuan taken from the farmland donation of 20% per mu in Huaiyang counties, and the remaining 400,000 yuan from the additional collection of 20% on canal cargo donations and the levy of canal shipping donations. The Jiangbei Canal Project Bureau was established, and in the ninth year of the Republic of China, the dredging bureau was reorganized into the Jiangsu Canal Project Bureau, which published a plan for the annual construction of the canal, with a budget of 3 million yuan. Unfortunately, the plan was never realized. In the 19th year of the Republic of China, the Canal Works Office was merged into the Water Conservancy Bureau of the Construction Department, resulting in its existence in name only, and the great disaster in Huaiyang began. Therefore, the Jiangbei Canal Project Aftermath Committee was born in response to the breach. However, this is only a plan for repairing the breach and the plan for managing the canal are two separate matters. The plan for managing the canal was announced more than ten years ago. Before the canal embankment collapsed last year, where were all the completed projects that could protect the counties in the lower reaches of the canal? Alas, the authorities treat water conservancy projects related to the national economy and the people's livelihood as child's play, or even as a source of profit, sweeping the people's blood and sweat into their own pockets. What responsibility should the so-called canal management experts bear? Will they use the outdated survey and mapping charts of empty talk to redeem our millions of lives and properties? Every time we think of the location of our ancestors' graves and the safety of our lives and properties, we are shocked and have to make plans to prevent future disasters. Therefore, based on our conscience, we jointly organize a group and plan to gather water conservancy engineers at home and abroad to research and improve, not to call for help after the event, but to plan in advance, so that the east and west embankments of our canal can have appropriate projects to protect our country, and then seek fundamental solutions. This is what we hope. In addition to separately formulating articles of association, discussing and resolving matters according to law, and submitting an application for registration, we hereby declare."

Overview of the American Bus Industry

News from the American Commercial Counselor's Office in China

The American bus industry is developing rapidly and occupies an important position in automobile transportation. Recently, the National Bus Association has been established, and the surge in buses, from only 10,000 in 1921 to 100,000 in 1931, is enough to show its rapid progress. Buses can be broadly divided into public and private. Public buses, such as long-distance buses, electric road buses, and steam road buses, are used exclusively for public transportation. Private buses, such as school buses, tour buses, hotels, and other businesses' buses. In 1931, the total number of buses in the United States was 98,000, with public buses accounting for slightly less than 50% and private buses accounting for slightly more than 50%. Electric tram companies in the United States have more than 12,000 buses to supplement their main electric tram business. Among private buses, approximately 48,500 are owned by schools and 3,000 are used for passenger tours. In 1931, public buses traveled 1,808,000,000 miles and carried 1,802,000,000 passengers. In that year, the government's income from this item reached 378,000,000 US dollars, and the investment amount reached 397,000,000 US dollars. Bus revenue was 300,000,000 US dollars in 1926 and 378,000,000 US dollars in 1931. However, at the same time, steam train revenue decreased from 1,000,000,000 US dollars to 555,000,000 US dollars, and electric train revenue decreased from approximately 950,000,000 US dollars to 750,000,000 US dollars. From this, we can see the rise and fall of buses and other transportation industries. The business of steam trains and electric trains relies on the branch lines of buses for promotion. However, the former's roads are shrinking and becoming shorter, while the latter's routes are increasing. The number of miles of highways in the United States is 3 million, of which 700,000 miles are bus routes. The total number of miles of highways in the world is 80,000 miles, and the total number of cars in the world is 35.6 million, with the United States accounting for 75% of them. Moreover, cars manufactured in the United States account for 87% of the world's total. This is a general overview. In the United States, there are more cars than telephones.

Local News Two

Summer Resort: Gaohang Beach

A Glimpse of Facilities and Transportation

Shanghai lacks the scenery of lakes and mountains. During the hot summer, those who are tied to their duties are busy all day long. Apart from taking walks in the park during public holidays, there are few places to relax and escape the heat. Especially during long, hot days on rest days, they are only trapped between mosquito swarms and sweat. Foreigners in Shanghai often go to the beach for a swim on their days off. The blue water, layered waves, sandy sails, wind gulls, floating and sinking among them, can filter out the mundane. In recent years, Chinese ladies have also been learning to swim. The Municipal Public Works Bureau has specially opened roads and arranged bathing beaches to promote national sports. Is it just for leisure and escaping the heat?

Facilities The bathing beach is located on the coast north of Gaohang Town in Pudong, with yellow sand like a belt and vast waves. The deepest part is only shoulder-deep. Even those who do not know how to swim can stand upright in the water. The shallow part is only ankle-deep. Red flags are planted all around the beach as markers. Beyond this, the sea water gradually deepens, and even those who can swim shallowly should not risk going forward. Behind the sandy shore, on the green grass, wooden houses are built and surrounded by blue and white canvas curtains. Inside, there are tables and chairs, as well as soda, beer, meals, candy, etc., for tourists to rest. There are also umbrellas and couches on the sandy shore for guests to sit on. On both sides of the house, there are more than ten wooden pavilions for changing clothes and washing, which are available for guests to use for six cents per room. The water basins and soap towels provided are very clean, but the lack of a shower after sea bathing is a regret. Swimsuits are also available for rent, but they are knitted. Those who are not used to swimming may easily catch a cold if they wear them, and there are not many available. It is better for visitors to prepare their own set, which is more suitable for use.

Transportation Although it takes three changes of boats and cars to get from Shanghai to the bathing beach, the Public Works Bureau has arranged everything well, so there is no suffering on the journey. Tourists first take the municipal ferry at the Bund Bronze Man Wharf. A special class costs half a yuan per person and goes directly to Gaohang. The ferry is the most well-equipped on the Huangpu River. The ferry seats are spacious and the cabins are clean. Upon landing at Gaohang, there are buses waiting there. The fare from the wharf to Gaohang Town is only one cent. After getting off the bus, you have to take a rickshaw. The Public Works Bureau stipulates that the fare is four cents per rickshaw ride, and staff are dispatched to direct the rickshaw drivers and serve as receptionists, so the order is orderly and convenient for tourists. The whole journey takes about two hours. If you take the first ferry (departing at 7:00 am), you can reach the bathing beach at about 9:00 am.

Chen Xing Accused of Abandonment

Yan Shufen Files an Appeal

The Hearing and Debate Concluded Yesterday

Chen Xing, courtesy name Jian'an, the general manager of the Central Bank, once hired Yan Shufen, the cousin of Yan Dunyuan, the former Minister of Internal Affairs of the Beijing government, as his wife. At that time, Chen was still studying in Shanghai and was very poor. He often had difficulty paying for tuition. Fortunately, his parents-in-law had keen eyes and knew that their future son-in-law was not an ordinary person. Therefore, they did not hesitate to spend money to cultivate him in the hope of making him successful. Chen also worked hard to improve himself. After graduating from a Shanghai school, he went abroad for further studies. Unexpectedly, in the autumn of his success, he forgot the kindness of his parents-in-law and left Shufen behind. He married Miss Cai and after returning to China, he did not treat her well. He left his fiancée alone in her boudoir, wasting her youth. Shufen is now forty-two years old. Last year, she filed a lawsuit against Chen for abandonment and other reasons, requesting a consolation payment of 100,000 yuan. At the beginning of the trial, Chen presented evidence proving that Shufen had married Fu Rui (courtesy name Wu Tui), the nephew of Fu Jiang (courtesy name Xie Chen), the former Shanghai Tao Yin, in the old capital. Although they separated on the wedding night, there was still a flaw and it was not appropriate to stay together for life. Therefore, the first instance resulted in Yan Shufen being defeated. However, the woman firmly denied marrying Fu, only admitting that because Chen had not married her for a long time and had repeatedly indicated that he wanted to break off the engagement, her parents had arranged for her to be engaged to Fu Rui. When the auspicious day arrived, the woman vowed not to serve two husbands and cut her hair to show her determination. The marriage contract was naturally terminated. Chen said that the wedding ceremony had been held, which was a malicious slander and damaged her reputation. She was very unwilling to accept this and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and specially invited Fu Wu Tui to come from the north to testify, proving that no wedding ceremony had been held that year. Since Miss Yan did not want to be my spouse, I had no choice but to give up and seek another partner. The judge then suspended the trial and advised both parties to reconcile outside the court. If it was difficult to reconcile, they should wait for Chen to be summoned to court for a continued trial. However, the suspension has lasted for several months and the peace talks have made no progress. Therefore, the Second High Court held a collegial panel hearing again yesterday morning. Chen Xing said that he had to attend the research meeting on abolishing the tael and changing the yuan and could not attend the court. His lawyer Zhang Zhirang appeared in court on his behalf. Lawyer Jiang said that the appellant had never arrived and this time he was summoned but still did not arrive for excuses, causing the case to be delayed again and again. Chen had previously been supported by the Yan family and there had been several witnesses to prove that he had been favored. Now there is Xu, who also knows about his gratitude and can testify. Then Xu detailed the story of the old lady's repeated financial assistance. Lawyer Jiang continued to present several letters from Chen to Yan Shufen after returning to China, saying that the words in the letters were all Chen's words of regret and there was no intention to break off the engagement. This shows that Chen could not fulfill the marriage contract and had other difficulties. The reason why he did not come to court in person was that he was ashamed of the appellant. After the two sides debated, the official ordered them to withdraw and wait for a scheduled verdict.

Married Daughter of a Comprador of a Foreign Firm Sues for Inheritance

Father Died and Younger Brother Died Early

Now Sues Her Brother's Wife

Sun Jingfu, courtesy name Jingchen, the comprador of the leasing department of the Pacific Foreign Firm, had been in office for more than 30 years and accumulated a lot of wealth. He was considered to be a well-off family. He died on August 4 last year. He had one son and two daughters. The eldest daughter, Ji Zhang, married Tao early. The youngest daughter, Yi Zhang, has not yet married. The son, Bin Xuan, died five years before his father. Fortunately, he had married Zhu Lingxian and left behind three sons, Wenliao, Wenlan, and Wenda, and one daughter, Hongyu. Tao Sun Ji Zhang, after her father Jingchen passed away, said that her father had a lot of inherited real estate, cash deposits, and shares. According to current laws, married daughters also have the right to inherit. Therefore, she repeatedly negotiated with her brother's wife, Sun Zhu Lingxian, requesting a share based on the shares. However, Zhu Lingxian said that the property in her possession was all purchased by her husband, Sun Bin Xuan, and did not come from her uncle. She refused to split it. Tao Sun was not willing to give up, and recently investigated her father's property clearly. As far as she knew, in terms of real estate, there were (1) houses and land in Chaoyangli, Tiandian Road, all registered by the Gao Yi Consulate, (2) 21 buildings of Chunfang City houses and a piece of vacant land on the north side of Elcock Road, and 13 and a half city houses on the south side, also registered by Gao Yi and leased by the Pacific Foreign Firm, (3) a residence in Changkangli, Dong Han Bili Road, two houses, and four city houses, (4) one city house on Yalu Road, (5) 2.67 mu of vacant land on Zhaofeng Road. Only Chaoyangli was jointly purchased with Chen Guangchang, Sun got three shares, and the rest were all purchased by him alone. In terms of deposits, there were (1) 25,000 taels in the Mercantile Bank, (2) 27,000 yuan in the Siming Bank, (3) approximately 20,100 taels in commercial deposits, (4) approximately 2,000 taels in current silver accounts, (5) approximately 2,000 yuan in current foreign accounts, (6) 23,000 yuan in mortgage from Wu Yaoting at 491 Huishan Road. In addition, there were 4,000 taels of Shanghai Municipal Council 6% bonds. The combined value of these two types of movable and immovable property should reach hundreds of thousands. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court, requesting that she be allowed to split the property equally with Sun Zhu's children. The petition also stated that her brother Bin Xuan had been suffering from hemoptysis for a long time and had never lived independently. How could he have the financial resources to purchase property? Sun Zhu intended to swallow it all and did not hesitate to reverse black and white. She should be thoroughly investigated and judged according to law to protect her rights. The case was originally scheduled to be heard by Judge Shen Hong yesterday morning, but due to time constraints, it could not be questioned, so a separate date must be set for a summons hearing.

Police Officer Dies in the Line of Duty

Zhang Hanchen Dies of Serious Injuries

The Authorities Should Provide Preferential Treatment

At 9:40 pm the night before, Sun Jiming, a patrol police officer from the Second District Municipal Public Security Bureau Branch, was patrolling with a Mauser pistol at the intersection of Xiejiao Liyuan Road and Xinqiao Road. Suddenly, three bandits shot the police officer in the left leg and snatched the Mauser pistol. At the same time, a police officer named Zhang Hanchen heard the alarm and rushed to assist in the arrest. He was also shot in the waist and other parts by the bandits. This has been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the two injured police officers were sent to Shanghai Hospital yesterday. Zhang Hanchen, the injured police officer, was in ward 6 of the fourth class of the hospital. Because the bullet hit his waist, his internal waist, lungs, and stomach were broken. He did not have time to be treated and died at 5 am yesterday. Xie Zhongyi, the police inspector of the Liyuan Road Branch, led Tong Patrol Captain and others to Shanghai Hospital at 11:30 am yesterday to prepare a coffin and collect the body, and then submit a request for preferential treatment. The patrol police officer Sun Jiming was shot through his left leg and his life is not in danger. Now, Zhang Dongkai, the district chief of the Second District, believes that the two bandits dared to rob police officers of their weapons and shoot and kill police officers. The matter is of great importance. He has ordered Han Ruisheng, the leader of the detective team, to supervise the detectives and strictly order them to arrest the suspects within ten days to solve the case.
